### Additional notes

A fairly rare case of an empty enum with a single-line comment inside. 

Formatting causes terminating brace on an enum to be a part of the comment. This doesn't seem to be the case for other similar declarations.

  1077	        let raw = self.raw().unwrap().as_str();
  1078	
  1079	        let Some((pattern, flags)) = raw.rsplit_once('/') else {
  1080	            return write!(f, text(raw));
  1081	        };
  1082	
  1083	        // Regex flags are ASCII and limited to at most 8 unique: d, g, i, m, s, u, v, y
  1084	        debug_assert!(flags.len() <= 8 && flags.is_ascii());
  1085	        let mut flags_buf = [0u8; 8];

  1087	        flags_buf[..len].copy_from_slice(flags.as_bytes());

  1330	        write!(f, [AssignmentLike::TSTypeAliasDeclaration(self), OptionalSemicolon]);
  1331	    }
  1332	}
  1333	
  1334	impl<'a> FormatWrite<'a> for AstNode<'a, TSInterfaceDeclaration<'a>> {
  1335	    fn write(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
  1336	        let id = self.id();
  1337	        let type_parameters = self.type_parameters();
  1338	        let extends = self.extends();
  1339	        let body = self.body();
  1340	
  1341	        // Determines whether to use group mode for formatting the `extends` clause.
  1342	        // 1. If there are multiple `extends`, we always use group mode.
  1343	        // 2. If there is a single `extends` that is a member expression without type arguments, we use group mode.
  1344	        // 3. If there are comments between the `id` and the `extends`, we use group mode.
  1345	        let group_mode = extends.len() > 1
  1346	            || extends.as_ref().first().is_some_and(|first| {
  1347	                (first.expression.is_member_expression() && first.type_arguments.is_none()) || {
  1348	                    let prev_span = type_parameters.as_ref().map_or(id.span(), GetSpan::span);
  1349	                    f.comments().has_comment_in_range(prev_span.end, first.span().start)
  1350	                }
  1351	            });
  1352	
  1353	        let format_id = format_with(|f| {
  1354	            if type_parameters.is_none() && extends.is_empty() {
  1355	                FormatNodeWithoutTrailingComments(id).fmt(f);
  1356	            } else {
  1357	                write!(f, [id]);
  1358	            }
  1359	
  1360	            if let Some(type_parameters) = type_parameters {
  1361	                let type_parameters_group = Some(f.group_id("type_parameters"));
  1362	                write!(
  1363	                    f,
  1364	                    FormatTSTypeParameters::new(
  1365	                        type_parameters,
  1366	                        FormatTSTypeParametersOptions {
  1367	                            group_id: type_parameters_group,
  1368	                            is_type_or_interface_decl: true
  1369	                        }
  1370	                    )
  1371	                );
  1372	            }
  1373	        });
  1374	
  1375	        let format_extends = format_with(|f| {
  1376	            let Some(first_extend) = extends.as_ref().first() else {
  1377	                return;
  1378	            };
  1379	
  1380	            let has_leading_own_line_comment =
  1381	                f.context().comments().has_leading_own_line_comment(first_extend.span().start);
  1382	
  1383	            if has_leading_own_line_comment {
  1384	                write!(
  1385	                    f,
  1386	                    FormatTrailingComments::Comments(
  1387	                        f.context().comments().comments_before(first_extend.span().start)
  1388	                    )
  1389	                );
  1390	            }
  1391	
  1392	            if extends.len() > 1 {
  1393	                write!(
  1394	                    f,
  1395	                    [
  1396	                        soft_line_break_or_space(),
  1397	                        "extends",
  1398	                        group(&soft_line_indent_or_space(extends))
  1399	                    ]
  1400	                );
  1401	            } else {
  1402	                let format_extends = format_with(|f| write!(f, ["extends", space(), extends]));
  1403	                if group_mode {
  1404	                    write!(f, [soft_line_break_or_space(), group(&format_extends)]);
  1405	                } else {
  1406	                    write!(f, [space(), format_extends]);
  1407	                }
  1408	            }
  1409	
  1410	            let has_leading_own_line_comment =
  1411	                f.context().comments().has_leading_own_line_comment(self.body.span().start);
  1412	
  1413	            if !has_leading_own_line_comment {
  1414	                write!(f, [space()]);
  1415	                body.format_leading_comments(f);
  1416	            }
  1417	        });
  1418	
  1419	        let content = format_with(|f| {
  1420	            if self.declare() {
  1421	                write!(f, ["declare", space()]);
  1422	            }
  1423	
  1424	            write!(f, ["interface", space()]);
  1425	
  1426	            if extends.is_empty() {
  1427	                write!(f, [format_id, format_extends]);
  1428	            } else if group_mode {
  1429	                let indented = format_with(|f| write!(f, [format_id, indent(&format_extends)]));
  1430	                let heritage_id = f.group_id("heritageGroup");
  1431	                write!(f, [group(&indented).with_group_id(Some(heritage_id)), space()]);
  1432	            } else {
  1433	                write!(f, [&format_args!(format_id, format_extends)]);
  1434	            }
  1435	
  1436	            write!(f, [space()]);
  1437	            // Avoid printing leading comments of body
  1438	            body.write(f);
  1439	        });
  1440	
  1441	        write!(f, group(&content));
  1442	    }
  1443	}
  1444	
  1445	impl<'a> FormatWrite<'a> for AstNode<'a, TSInterfaceBody<'a>> {
  1446	    fn write(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
  1447	        write!(f, [space(), "{"]);
  1448	
  1449	        if self.body.is_empty() {
  1450	            write!(f, format_dangling_comments(self.span).with_block_indent());
  1451	        } else {
  1452	            write!(f, block_indent(&self.body()));
  1453	        }
  1454	
  1455	        write!(f, "}");
  1456	    }
  1457	}
  1458	
  1459	impl<'a> FormatWrite<'a> for AstNode<'a, TSPropertySignature<'a>> {
  1460	    fn write(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
  1461	        if self.readonly() {
  1462	            write!(f, ["readonly", space()]);
  1463	        }
  1464	        if self.computed() {
  1465	            write!(f, ["[", self.key(), "]"]);

    16	#[derive(Clone, Copy)]
    17	pub enum ObjectLike<'a, 'b> {
    18	    ObjectExpression(&'b AstNode<'a, ObjectExpression<'a>>),
    19	    TSTypeLiteral(&'b AstNode<'a, TSTypeLiteral<'a>>),
    20	}
    21	
    22	impl<'a> ObjectLike<'a, '_> {
    23	    fn span(&self) -> Span {
    24	        match self {
    25	            ObjectLike::ObjectExpression(o) => o.span,
    26	            ObjectLike::TSTypeLiteral(o) => o.span,
    27	        }
    28	    }
    29	
    30	    fn should_hug(&self, f: &Formatter<'_, 'a>) -> bool {
    31	        // Check if the object type is the type annotation of the only parameter in a function.
    32	        // This prevents breaking object properties in cases like:
    33	        // const fn = ({ foo }: { foo: string }) => { ... };
    34	        matches!(self, Self::TSTypeLiteral(node) if {
    35	            // Check if parent is TSTypeAnnotation
    36	            matches!(node.parent(), AstNodes::TSTypeAnnotation(type_ann) if {
    37	                match &type_ann.parent() {
    38	                    AstNodes::FormalParameter(param) if param.initializer.is_none() => {
    39	                        let AstNodes::FormalParameters(parameters) = &param.parent() else {
    40	                            unreachable!()
    41	                        };
    42	                        let this_param = get_this_param(parameters.parent());
    43	                        should_hug_function_parameters(parameters, this_param, false, f)
    44	
    45	                    }
    46	                    AstNodes::TSThisParameter(param) => {
    47	                        matches!(param.parent(), AstNodes::Function(func) if {
    48	                            should_hug_function_parameters(func.params(), Some(param), false, f)
    49	                        })
    50	                    },
    51	                    _ => false,
    52	                }
    53	            })
    54	        })
    55	    }
    56	
    57	    fn members_have_leading_newline(&self, f: &Formatter<'_, 'a>) -> bool {
    58	        match self {
    59	            Self::ObjectExpression(o) => o.as_ref().properties.first().is_some_and(|p| {
    60	                f.source_text().contains_newline_between(o.span.start, p.span().start)
    61	            }),
    62	            Self::TSTypeLiteral(o) => o.as_ref().members.first().is_some_and(|p| {
    63	                f.source_text().contains_newline_between(o.span().start, p.span().start)
    64	            }),
    65	        }
    66	    }
    67	
    68	    fn members_are_empty(&self) -> bool {
    69	        match self {
    70	            Self::ObjectExpression(o) => o.properties().is_empty(),
    71	            Self::TSTypeLiteral(o) => o.members().is_empty(),
    72	        }
    73	    }
    74	
    75	    /// Check if the object is inside a JSX spread attribute or JSX spread child.
    76	    /// In these contexts, empty objects with comments should use soft line breaks
    77	    /// so they can stay on one line if they fit.
    78	    fn is_inside_jsx_spread(&self) -> bool {
    79	        match self {
    80	            Self::ObjectExpression(o) => {
    81	                matches!(o.parent(), AstNodes::JSXSpreadAttribute(_) | AstNodes::JSXSpreadChild(_))
    82	            }
    83	            Self::TSTypeLiteral(_) => false,
    84	        }
    85	    }
    86	
    87	    fn write_members(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
    88	        match self {
    89	            Self::ObjectExpression(o) => o.properties().fmt(f),
    90	            Self::TSTypeLiteral(o) => o.members().fmt(f),
    91	        }
    92	    }
    93	}
    94	
    95	impl<'a> Format<'a> for ObjectLike<'a, '_> {
    96	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
    97	        let members = format_with(|f| self.write_members(f));
    98	
    99	        write!(f, "{");
   100	
   101	        if self.members_are_empty() {
   102	            // In JSX spread attributes/children, use soft indent so the object
   103	            // can stay on one line if it fits (e.g., `<div {...{/* comment */}} />`).
   104	            // In other contexts like variable declarations, use block indent to
   105	            // expand the object (e.g., `var a = {\n  /* comment */\n};`).
   106	            if self.is_inside_jsx_spread() {
   107	                write!(f, format_dangling_comments(self.span()).with_soft_block_indent());
   108	            } else {
   109	                write!(f, format_dangling_comments(self.span()).with_block_indent());
   110	            }
   111	        } else {
   112	            let should_insert_space_around_brackets = f.options().bracket_spacing.value();
   113	            let should_expand =
   114	                f.options().expand == Expand::Auto && self.members_have_leading_newline(f);
   115	
   116	            // If the object type is the type annotation of the only parameter in a function,
   117	            // try to hug the parameter; we don't create a group and inline the contents here.
   118	            //
   119	            // For example:
   120	            // ```ts
   121	            // const fn = ({ foo }: { foo: string }) => { ... };
   122	            //                      ^ do not break properties here
   123	            // ```
   124	            let should_hug = self.should_hug(f);
   125	
   126	            let inner =
   127	                soft_block_indent_with_maybe_space(&members, should_insert_space_around_brackets);
   128	
   129	            if should_hug {
   130	                write!(f, inner);
   131	            } else {
   132	                write!(f, [group(&inner).should_expand(should_expand)]);
   133	            }
   134	        }
   135	
   136	        write!(f, "}");
   137	    }
   138	}

#![allow(clippy::inline_always, clippy::missing_panics_doc)] // FIXME: all these needs to be fixed.

pub use crate::ast_nodes::{AstNode, AstNodes};
pub use crate::external_formatter::{
    EmbeddedDocFormatterCallback, EmbeddedDocResult, EmbeddedFormatterCallback, ExternalCallbacks,
    TailwindCallback,
};
pub use crate::formatter::format_element::tag::{
    Align, Condition, DedentMode, Group, GroupMode, Tag,
};
pub use crate::formatter::format_element::{
    BestFittingElement, FormatElement, LineMode, PrintMode, TextWidth,
};

pub use crate::options::*;

pub use crate::service::*;

#[cfg(feature = "detect_code_removal")]
pub use detect_code_removal::detect_code_removal;

use self::formatter::prelude::tag::Label;

pub struct Formatter<'a> {
    allocator: &'a Allocator,
    options: FormatOptions,
}

impl<'a> Formatter<'a> {
    pub fn new(allocator: &'a Allocator, options: FormatOptions) -> Self {
        Self { allocator, options }
    }

    /// Formats the given AST `Program` and returns the formatted string.
    pub fn build(self, program: &Program<'a>) -> String {
        let formatted = self.format(program);
        formatted.print().unwrap().into_code()
    }

    #[inline]
    pub fn format(self, program: &'a Program<'a>) -> Formatted<'a> {
        self.format_with_external_callbacks(program, None)
    }

    #[inline]
    pub fn format_with_external_callbacks(
        self,
        program: &'a Program<'a>,
        external_callbacks: Option<ExternalCallbacks>,
    ) -> Formatted<'a> {
        let program_node = AstNode::new(program, AstNodes::Dummy(), self.allocator);

        let context = FormatContext::new(
            program.source_text,
            program.source_type,
            &program.comments,
            self.allocator,
            self.options,
            external_callbacks,
        );

        let mut formatted = formatter::format(
            context,
            formatter::Arguments::new(&[formatter::Argument::new(&program_node)]),
        );

        // Basic formatting and `document.propagate_expand()` are already done here.
        // Now apply additional transforms if enabled.
        if let Some(sort_imports_options) = &formatted.context().options().sort_imports
            && let Some(transformed_elements) = SortImportsTransform::transform(
                formatted.document(),
                sort_imports_options,
                self.allocator,
            )
        {
            formatted.document_mut().replace_elements(transformed_elements);
        }

        formatted
    }

    /// Formats an arbitrary value that implements `Format` and returns the `Formatted` IR.
    ///
    /// Unlike `format()` which requires a full `Program`,
    /// this method accepts any value that implements `Format`.
    /// This enables fragment formatting for embedded contexts like:
    /// - Vue: `v-for`, `v-slot`, and `<script generic="...">`
    /// - etc...
    ///
    /// `SortImportsTransform` is skipped since it only applies to whole `Program` formatting.
    pub fn format_node<F: formatter::Format<'a>>(
        self,
        node: &F,
        source_text: &'a str,
        source_type: SourceType,
        comments: &'a [Comment],
        external_callbacks: Option<ExternalCallbacks>,
    ) -> Formatted<'a> {
        let context = FormatContext::new(
            source_text,
            source_type,
            comments,
            self.allocator,
            self.options,
            external_callbacks,
        );
        formatter::format(context, formatter::Arguments::new(&[formatter::Argument::new(node)]))
    }
}

#[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]
pub(crate) enum JsLabels {
    MemberChain,
    /// For `ir_transform/sort_imports`
    ImportDeclaration,
    /// For `ir_transform/sort_imports`
    /// Marks `alignable_comment` (Block comment where each line starts with `*`)
    /// to distinguish from other text content like template literals that may contain `/*`.
    AlignableBlockComment,
}

     4	//! This example demonstrates how to use the Oxc formatter to format JavaScript and TypeScript code.
     5	//!
     6	//! ## Usage
     7	//!
     8	//! Create a `test.js` file and run:
     9	//! ```bash
    10	//! cargo run -p oxc_formatter --example formatter [filename]
    11	//! cargo run -p oxc_formatter --example formatter -- --no-semi [filename]
    12	//! cargo run -p oxc_formatter --example formatter -- --jsdoc [filename]
    13	//! cargo run -p oxc_formatter --example formatter -- --diff [filename]

    16	use std::{fs, path::Path};
    17	
    18	use oxc_allocator::Allocator;
    19	use oxc_formatter::{
    20	    BracketSameLine, FormatOptions, Formatter, JsdocOptions, LineWidth, Semicolons,
    21	    get_parse_options,
    22	};
    23	use oxc_parser::Parser;
    24	use oxc_span::SourceType;
    25	use oxc_tasks_common::print_diff_in_terminal;
    26	use pico_args::Arguments;
    27	
    28	/// Format a JavaScript or TypeScript file
    29	fn main() -> Result<(), String> {
    30	    let mut args = Arguments::from_env();
    31	    let no_semi = args.contains("--no-semi");
    32	    let jsdoc = args.contains("--jsdoc");
    33	    let show_ir = args.contains("--ir");
    34	    // Show diff between original and formatted code
    35	    let show_diff = args.contains("--diff");
    36	    let print_width = args.opt_value_from_str::<&'static str, u16>("--print-width").unwrap_or(None);
    37	    let name = args.free_from_str().unwrap_or_else(|_| "test.js".to_string());
    38	
    39	    // Read source file
    40	    let path = Path::new(&name);
    41	    let source_text = fs::read_to_string(path).map_err(|_| format!("Missing '{name}'"))?;
    42	    let source_type = SourceType::from_path(path).unwrap();
    43	
    44	    // Format the parsed code
    45	    let semicolons = if no_semi { Semicolons::AsNeeded } else { Semicolons::Always };
    46	    let line_width = match print_width {
    47	        Some(width) => LineWidth::try_from(width).unwrap(),
    48	        None => LineWidth::try_from(80).unwrap(),
    49	    };
    50	    let jsdoc_options = if jsdoc { Some(JsdocOptions::default()) } else { None };
    51	    let options = FormatOptions {
    52	        bracket_same_line: BracketSameLine::from(true),
    53	        semicolons,
    54	        line_width,
    55	        jsdoc: jsdoc_options,
    56	        ..Default::default()
    57	    };
    58	
    59	    let allocator = Allocator::new();
    60	
    61	    // Parse the source code
    62	    let ret = Parser::new(&allocator, &source_text, source_type)
    63	        .with_options(get_parse_options())
    64	        .parse();
    65	
    66	    // Report any parsing errors
    67	    for error in ret.errors {
    68	        let error = error.with_source_code(source_text.clone());
    69	        println!("{error:?}");
    70	        println!("Parsed with Errors.");
    71	    }
    72	
    73	    let formatted = Formatter::new(&allocator, options).format(&ret.program);
    74	
    75	    if show_ir {
    76	        println!("--- IR ---");
    77	        println!("{}", &formatted.document().to_string());
    78	        println!("--- End IR ---\n");
    79	    }
    80	
    81	    let formatted_code = formatted.print().unwrap().into_code();
    82	
    83	    if show_diff {
    84	        // First diff: compare formatted output to original input
    85	        if source_text == formatted_code {
    86	            println!("{formatted_code}");
    87	        } else {
    88	            print_diff_in_terminal(&source_text, &formatted_code);
    89	        }
    90	    } else {
    91	        // println!("--- Formatted Code ---");
    92	        // println!("{formatted_code}");
    93	        // println!("--- End Formatted Code ---");
    94	    }
    95	
    96	    Ok(())
    97	}

     1	//! High-level comment formatting interface for the on-demand comment system.
     2	//!
     3	//! This module provides the formatting implementations that work with the cursor-based
     4	//! comment tracking system in [`crate::formatter::comments`]. It handles the actual
     5	//! rendering of comments with proper spacing, line breaks, and indentation.
     6	//!
     7	//! ## Integration with Comment Architecture
     8	//!
     9	//! This module is the "formatting layer" of our on-demand comment system:
    10	//!
    11	//! 1. **AST formatting code calls** the format functions in this module
    12	//! 2. **These functions query** the comment system for relevant comments
    13	//! 3. **Comments are formatted** with appropriate spacing and breaks
    14	//! 4. **The cursor is advanced** to mark comments as processed
    15	//!
    16	//! ## Comment Formatting Implementation
    17	//!
    18	//! ### Leading Comment Formatting ([`FormatLeadingComments`])
    19	//! ```rust,ignore
    20	//! // In AST node formatting:
    21	//! write!(f, [format_leading_comments(node.span)]);
    22	//! write!(f, [node]);
    23	//! ```
    24	//!
    25	//! **Implementation**:
    26	//! 1. Calls `comments_before(node.span.start)` to get unprinted leading comments
    27	//! 2. Formats each comment with spacing based on line breaks in original source
    28	//! 3. Advances cursor by calling `increment_printed_count()` for each comment
    29	//! 4. Handles special cases like JSDoc comment "nestling"
    30	//!
    31	//! ### Trailing Comment Formatting ([`FormatTrailingComments`])
    32	//! ```rust,ignore
    33	//! // In AST node formatting:
    34	//! write!(f, [node]);
    35	//! write!(f, [format_trailing_comments(enclosing, preceding, following)]);
    36	//! ```
    37	//!
    38	//! **Implementation**:
    39	//! 1. Calls `get_trailing_comments()` with node context to determine ownership
    40	//! 2. Uses line suffixes to prevent comments from interfering with code layout
    41	//! 3. Handles complex spacing rules for different comment types
    42	//! 4. Advances cursor after processing each comment
    43	//!
    44	//! ### Dangling Comment Formatting ([`FormatDanglingComments`])
    45	//! ```rust,ignore
    46	//! // In container node formatting:
    47	//! write!(f, [
    48	//!     "{",
    49	//!     format_dangling_comments(container.span).with_block_indent(),
    50	//!     "}"
    51	//! ]);
    52	//! ```
    53	//!
    54	//! **Implementation**:
    55	//! 1. Calls `comments_between()` to find internal comments not owned by children
    56	//! 2. Applies indentation based on container type (block, soft, none)
    57	//! 3. Preserves comment relationships and spacing
    58	//! 4. Advances cursor for processed comments

    62	use oxc_syntax::line_terminator::LineTerminatorSplitter;

    64	use crate::{JsLabels, write};

    68	/// Returns true if:
    69	/// - `next_comment` is Some, and
    70	/// - both comments are documentation comments, and
    71	/// - both comments are multiline, and
    72	/// - the two comments are immediately adjacent to each other, with no characters between them.
    73	///
    74	/// In this case, the comments are considered "nestled" - a pattern that JSDoc uses to represent
    75	/// overloaded types, which get merged together to create the final type for the subject. The
    76	/// comments must be kept immediately adjacent after formatting to preserve this behavior.
    77	///
    78	/// There isn't much documentation about this behavior, but it is mentioned on the JSDoc repo
    79	/// for documentation: <https://github.com/jsdoc/jsdoc.github.io/issues/40>. Prettier also
    80	/// implements the same behavior: <https://github.com/prettier/prettier/pull/13445/files#diff-3d5eaa2a1593372823589e6e55e7ca905f7c64203ecada0aa4b3b0cdddd5c3ddR160-R178>
    81	fn should_nestle_adjacent_doc_comments(current: &Comment, next: &Comment) -> bool {
    82	    matches!(current.content, CommentContent::Jsdoc)
    83	        && matches!(next.content, CommentContent::Jsdoc)
    84	        && current.is_multiline_block()
    85	        && next.is_multiline_block()
    86	        && current.span.end == next.span.start
    87	}
    88	
    89	/// Formats the leading comments of `node`
    90	#[inline]
    91	pub const fn format_leading_comments<'a>(span: Span) -> FormatLeadingComments<'a> {
    92	    FormatLeadingComments::Node(span)
    93	}
    94	
    95	/// Formats the leading comments of a node.
    96	#[derive(Debug, Copy, Clone)]
    97	pub enum FormatLeadingComments<'a> {
    98	    Node(Span),
    99	    Comments(&'a [Comment]),
   100	}
   101	
   102	impl<'a> Format<'a> for FormatLeadingComments<'a> {
   103	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
   104	        fn format_leading_comments_impl<'a>(
   105	            comments: impl IntoIterator<Item = &'a Comment>,
   106	            f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>,
   107	        ) {
   108	            let mut leading_comments_iter = comments.into_iter().peekable();
   109	            while let Some(comment) = leading_comments_iter.next() {
   110	                f.context_mut().comments_mut().increment_printed_count();
   111	                write!(f, comment);
   112	
   113	                match comment.kind {
   114	                    CommentKind::SingleLineBlock | CommentKind::MultiLineBlock => {
   115	                        match f.source_text().lines_after(comment.span.end) {
   116	                            0 => {
   117	                                let should_nestle =
   118	                                    leading_comments_iter.peek().is_some_and(|next_comment| {
   119	                                        should_nestle_adjacent_doc_comments(comment, next_comment)
   120	                                    });
   121	
   122	                                write!(f, [maybe_space(!should_nestle)]);
   123	                            }
   124	                            1 => {
   125	                                if f.source_text().get_lines_before(comment.span, f.comments()) == 0
   126	                                {
   127	                                    write!(f, [soft_line_break_or_space()]);
   128	                                } else {
   129	                                    write!(f, [hard_line_break()]);
   130	                                }
   131	                            }
   132	                            _ => write!(f, [empty_line()]),
   133	                        }
   134	                    }
   135	                    CommentKind::Line => match f.source_text().lines_after(comment.span.end) {
   136	                        0 | 1 => write!(f, [hard_line_break()]),
   137	                        _ => write!(f, [empty_line()]),
   138	                    },
   139	                }
   140	            }
   141	        }
   142	
   143	        match self {
   144	            Self::Node(span) => {
   145	                let leading_comments = f.context().comments().comments_before(span.start);
   146	                if leading_comments.is_empty() {
   147	                    return;
   148	                }
   149	                format_leading_comments_impl(leading_comments, f);
   150	            }
   151	            Self::Comments(comments) => {
   152	                if comments.is_empty() {
   153	                    return;
   154	                }
   155	                format_leading_comments_impl(*comments, f);
   156	            }
   157	        }
   158	    }
   159	}

   171	/// Formats the trailing comments of `node`
   172	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy)]
   173	pub enum FormatTrailingComments<'a> {
   174	    // (enclosing_span, preceding_span, following_span_start)
   175	    Node((Span, Span, u32)),
   176	    Comments(&'a [Comment]),
   177	}
   178	
   179	impl<'a> Format<'a> for FormatTrailingComments<'a> {
   180	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
   181	        fn format_trailing_comments_impl<'a>(
   182	            comments: impl IntoIterator<Item = &'a Comment>,
   183	            f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>,
   184	        ) {
   185	            let mut total_lines_before = 0;
   186	            let mut previous_comment: Option<&Comment> = None;
   187	
   188	            for comment in comments {
   189	                f.context_mut().comments_mut().increment_printed_count();
   190	
   191	                let lines_before = f.source_text().get_lines_before(comment.span, f.comments());
   192	                total_lines_before += lines_before;
   193	
   194	                let should_nestle = previous_comment.is_some_and(|previous_comment| {
   195	                    should_nestle_adjacent_doc_comments(previous_comment, comment)
   196	                });
   197	
   198	                // This allows comments at the end of nested structures:
   199	                // {
   200	                //   x: 1,
   201	                //   y: 2
   202	                //   // A comment
   203	                // }
   204	                // Those kinds of comments are almost always leading comments, but
   205	                // here it doesn't go "outside" the block and turns it into a
   206	                // trailing comment for `2`. We can simulate the above by checking
   207	                // if this a comment on its own line; normal trailing comments are
   208	                // always at the end of another expression.
   209	                if total_lines_before > 0
   210	                    || previous_comment.is_some_and(|comment| comment.is_line())
   211	                {
   212	                    write!(
   213	                        f,
   214	                        [line_suffix(&format_with(|f| {
   215	                            match lines_before {
   216	                                _ if should_nestle => {}
   217	                                0 => {

   219	                                    // then it can stay on the same line with just a space between.
   220	                                    // Otherwise, it gets a hard break.
   221	                                    //
   222	                                    //   [>* hello <] // hi
   223	                                    //   [>*
   224	                                    //    * docs
   225	                                    //   */ [> still on the same line <]
   226	                                    if previous_comment.copied().is_some_and(Comment::is_line) {
   227	                                        write!(f, [hard_line_break()]);
   228	                                    } else {
   229	                                        write!(f, [space()]);
   230	                                    }
   231	                                }
   232	                                1 => write!(f, [hard_line_break()]),
   233	                                _ => write!(f, [empty_line()]),
   234	                            }
   235	
   236	                            write!(f, [comment]);
   237	                        }))]
   238	                    );
   239	                } else {
   240	                    let content =

   279	/// Formats the dangling comments of `node`.
   280	#[inline]
   281	pub const fn format_dangling_comments<'a>(span: Span) -> FormatDanglingComments<'a> {
   282	    FormatDanglingComments::Node { span, indent: DanglingIndentMode::None }

   285	/// Formats the dangling trivia of `token`.
   286	pub enum FormatDanglingComments<'a> {
   287	    Node { span: Span, indent: DanglingIndentMode },
   288	    Comments { comments: &'a [Comment], indent: DanglingIndentMode },
   289	}
   290	
   291	#[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]
   292	pub enum DanglingIndentMode {
   293	    /// Writes every comment on its own line and indents them with a block indent.
   294	    ///
   295	    /// # Examples
   296	    /// ```ignore
   297	    /// [
   298	    ///     /* comment */
   299	    /// ]
   300	    ///
   301	    /// [
   302	    ///     /* comment */
   303	    ///     /* multiple */
   304	    /// ]
   305	    /// ```
   306	    Block,
   307	
   308	    /// Writes every comment on its own line and indents them with a soft line indent.
   309	    /// Guarantees to write a line break if the last formatted comment is a [line](CommentKind::Line) comment.
   310	    ///
   311	    /// # Examples
   312	    ///
   313	    /// ```ignore
   314	    /// [/* comment */]
   315	    ///
   316	    /// [
   317	    ///     /* comment */
   318	    ///     /* other */
   319	    /// ]
   320	    ///
   321	    /// [
   322	    ///     // line
   323	    /// ]
   324	    /// ```
   325	    Soft,
   326	
   327	    /// Writes every comment on its own line.
   328	    None,
   329	}
   330	
   331	impl FormatDanglingComments<'_> {
   332	    /// Indents the comments with a [block](DanglingIndentMode::Block) indent.
   333	    pub fn with_block_indent(self) -> Self {
   334	        self.with_indent_mode(DanglingIndentMode::Block)
   335	    }
   336	
   337	    /// Indents the comments with a [soft block](DanglingIndentMode::Soft) indent.
   338	    pub fn with_soft_block_indent(self) -> Self {
   339	        self.with_indent_mode(DanglingIndentMode::Soft)
   340	    }
   341	
   342	    fn with_indent_mode(mut self, mode: DanglingIndentMode) -> Self {
   343	        match &mut self {
   344	            FormatDanglingComments::Node { indent, .. }
   345	            | FormatDanglingComments::Comments { indent, .. } => *indent = mode,
   346	        }
   347	        self
   348	    }
   349	}
   350	
   351	impl<'a> Format<'a> for FormatDanglingComments<'a> {
   352	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
   353	        fn format_dangling_comments_impl<'a>(
   354	            comments: impl IntoIterator<Item = &'a Comment>,
   355	            indent: DanglingIndentMode,
   356	            f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>,
   357	        ) {
   358	            // Write all comments up to the first skipped token trivia or the token
   359	            let format_dangling_comments = format_once(|f| {
   360	                let mut previous_comment: Option<&Comment> = None;
   361	
   362	                for comment in comments {
   363	                    f.context_mut().comments_mut().increment_printed_count();
   364	
   365	                    let should_nestle = previous_comment.is_some_and(|previous_comment| {
   366	                        should_nestle_adjacent_doc_comments(previous_comment, comment)
   367	                    });
   368	
   369	                    write!(
   370	                        f,
   371	                        [
   372	                            (previous_comment.is_some() && !should_nestle)
   373	                                .then_some(hard_line_break()),
   374	                            comment
   375	                        ]
   376	                    );
   377	
   378	                    previous_comment = Some(comment);
   379	                }
   380	
   381	                if matches!(indent, DanglingIndentMode::Soft)
   382	                    && previous_comment.copied().is_some_and(Comment::is_line)
   383	                {
   384	                    write!(f, [hard_line_break()]);
   385	                }
   386	            });
   387	
   388	            match indent {
   389	                DanglingIndentMode::Block => {
   390	                    write!(f, [block_indent(&format_dangling_comments)]);
   391	                }
   392	                DanglingIndentMode::Soft => {
   393	                    write!(f, [group(&soft_block_indent(&format_dangling_comments))]);
   394	                }
   395	                DanglingIndentMode::None => {
   396	                    write!(f, [format_dangling_comments]);
   397	                }
   398	            }
   399	        }
   400	
   401	        match self {
   402	            FormatDanglingComments::Node { span, indent } => {
   403	                let dangling_comments = f.context().comments().comments_before(span.end);
   404	                if dangling_comments.is_empty() {
   405	                    return;
   406	                }
   407	                format_dangling_comments_impl(dangling_comments, *indent, f);
   408	            }
   409	            FormatDanglingComments::Comments { comments, indent } => {
   410	                if comments.is_empty() {
   411	                    return;
   412	                }
   413	                format_dangling_comments_impl(*comments, *indent, f);
   414	            }
   415	        }
   416	    }
   417	}
   418	
   419	impl<'a> Format<'a> for Comment {
   420	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
   421	        // JSDoc formatting: if enabled, try to format JSDoc comments
   422	        if self.is_jsdoc()
   423	            && !self.is_legal()
   424	            && let Some(jsdoc_options) = &f.options().jsdoc
   425	        {
   426	            let source: &str = &f.source_text();
   427	            let line_width = f.options().line_width.value() as usize;
   428	            // Calculate indent by counting whitespace immediately before the comment,
   429	            // walking backward and stopping at the first non-whitespace character.
   430	            // This matches upstream prettier-plugin-jsdoc's `getIndentationWidth()`:
   431	            //   for (let i = comment.loc.start.column - 1; i >= 0; i--) {
   432	            //     if (c === " ") spaces++; else if (c === "\t") tabs++; else break;
   433	            //   }
   434	            // For standalone comments (start of line), this equals the full indent.
   435	            // For inline comments (mid-expression, e.g. `? /** @type */`), this only
   436	            // counts the adjacent whitespace, giving more room for the comment content
   437	            // and preventing unnecessary type wrapping.
   438	            let indent_chars = {
   439	                let start = self.span.start as usize;
   440	                let before = &source[..start];
   441	                let tab_width = f.options().indent_width.value() as usize;
   442	                before
   443	                    .bytes()
   444	                    .rev()
   445	                    .take_while(|&b| b == b' ' || b == b'\t')
   446	                    .map(|b| if b == b'\t' { tab_width } else { 1 })
   447	                    .sum::<usize>()
   448	            };
   449	            let available_width = line_width.saturating_sub(indent_chars);
   450	            if let Some(formatted) =
   451	                super::jsdoc::format_jsdoc_comment(self, jsdoc_options, source, available_width, f)
   452	            {
   453	                write!(f, [formatted]);
   454	                return;
   455	            }
   456	        }
   457	
   458	        let content = f.source_text().text_for(&self.span);
   459	        if self.is_multiline_block() {
   460	            let mut lines = LineTerminatorSplitter::new(content);
   461	            if is_alignable_comment(content) {
   462	                // Using `write_element` directly instead of `labelled()`
   463	                // to avoid allocating a `Vec` for `lines` iter
   464	                let sort_imports_enabled = f.options().sort_imports.is_some();
   465	                if sort_imports_enabled {
   466	                    f.write_element(FormatElement::Tag(Tag::StartLabelled(LabelId::of(
   467	                        JsLabels::AlignableBlockComment,
   468	                    ))));
   469	                }
   470	
   471	                // `unwrap` is safe because `content` contains at least one line.
   472	                let first_line = lines.next().unwrap();
   473	                write!(f, [text(first_line.trim_end())]);
   474	
   475	                // Indent the remaining lines by one space so that all `*` are aligned.
   476	                for line in lines {
   477	                    write!(f, [hard_line_break(), " ", text(line.trim())]);
   478	                }
   479	
   480	                if sort_imports_enabled {
   481	                    f.write_element(FormatElement::Tag(Tag::EndLabelled));
   482	                }
   483	            } else {
   484	                // Normalize line endings `\r\n` to `\n`
   485	                let mut string = StringBuilder::with_capacity_in(content.len(), f.allocator());
   486	                // `unwrap` is safe because `content` contains at least one line.
   487	                string.push_str(lines.next().unwrap().trim_end());
   488	
   489	                for str in lines {
   490	                    string.push('\n');
   491	                    string.push_str(str);
   492	                }
   493	                write!(f, [text(string.into_str())]);
   494	            }
   495	        } else {
   496	            write!(f, [text(content.trim_end())]);
   497	        }
   498	    }
   499	}
   500

   515	///     /*
   516	///      * Single star
   517	///      */
   518	/// "#)));
   519	///
   520	///

  1302	#[derive(Copy, Clone)]
  1303	pub struct BlockIndent<'fmt, 'ast> {
  1304	    content: Argument<'fmt, 'ast>,
  1305	    mode: IndentMode,
  1306	}
  1307	
  1308	#[derive(Copy, Clone, Eq, PartialEq, Debug)]
  1309	enum IndentMode {
  1310	    Soft,
  1311	    Block,
  1312	    SoftSpace,
  1313	    SoftLineOrSpace,
  1314	}
  1315	
  1316	impl<'ast> Format<'ast> for BlockIndent<'_, 'ast> {
  1317	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'ast>) {
  1318	        f.write_element(FormatElement::Tag(StartIndent));
  1319	
  1320	        match self.mode {
  1321	            IndentMode::Soft => write!(f, soft_line_break()),
  1322	            IndentMode::Block => write!(f, hard_line_break()),
  1323	            IndentMode::SoftLineOrSpace | IndentMode::SoftSpace => {
  1324	                write!(f, soft_line_break_or_space());
  1325	            }
  1326	        }
  1327	
  1328	        let elements_length = f.elements().len();
  1329	
  1330	        Arguments::from(&self.content).fmt(f);
  1331	
  1332	        debug_assert_ne!(
  1333	            elements_length,
  1334	            f.elements().len(),
  1335	            "BlockIndent's content must produce at least one element"
